Still, I didn't connect the dots, and didn't realise I was in labour, so happily sent your dad off to town to buy bread. That's a 1 hour drive each way. So when he came back, your grandma, S√∏lvi, who lived in the same apartments at the time, was in one hundred thousand panic mode. Nothing unusual, she gets into that mode 5 seconds after she starts looking for her keys in her purse. Every. Time. But even I was a bit eager to set off to the hospital when he got back, another 2 hour drive. By then I knew you were coming. We drove up in his big red Mercedes, the only time I've driven without a seat belt, as by then, I could NOT sit still. And then he stopped at a gas station for cigarettes. I remember pacing back and forth outside, it seemed to take forever. Finally we get to the hospital, I waddle up to the birth suites on....5th floor I think. I remember looking out the window on our birth room, and we were high up, looking out at some tall, spindly pines with soggy wet but thick snow on the branches. I got helped out of my clothes, into a hospital gown, onto a bed, and at THAT moment my water broke. You were very polite. From that moment it was just a bunch of pushing for like 4 hours I think. We arrived around 1pm'ish at the hospital, and you plopped out around 5'ish. I can only remember it hurting for two contractions, when your head breached, until it came out. I got you up onto my chest first of all, umbilical cord still attached, not cleaned up. Someone put a blanket over you (and a hat maybe?) and I got to nuzzle you while your dad cut the cord. From then on I didn't want to let you go for even a moment. I didn't let you out of my sight for the whole duration of our hospital stay. I remember I brought a royal blue one piece with sailor details for bringing you home with. It was so soft, and still you were softer. That piece of clothing was so tiny, it never fit you again, only for that one trip to the hospital.
